The Miracles of Saints: Possibility and Occurrence
Definition and proof of the possibility and occurrence of saintly miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on the permissibility and actual occurrence of saintly miracles, and the proof based on divine power and the story of Mary.

Core Idea
God's unlimited power makes saintly miracles possible; Mary's story proves they occur.

The ninth section of al-Mawaqif addresses a debated topic: can saints perform miracles? The Ash'ari school affirms both the possibility and actual occurrence of such miracles. In this passage, the author states the position, notes opposing views, and provides two lines of proof: one from divine omnipotence and one from a scriptural example.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the opening statement that saintly miracles are permissible and occur.
The author uses 'jawāz' for permissibility and 'wuqūʿ' for occurrence.
2
Understand the disagreement
The passage mentions that some groups deny these miracles. Note the names: al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq, al-Halimi, and some Mu'tazila. This sets up the need for proof.
3
Examine the proof for permissibility
The proof is based on Ash'ari principles: all possible things depend on God's power, which has no limits. A miracle is a possible thing, so it is not impossible. No purpose is necessary.
This shows that the Ash'ari view on divine attributes (power, lack of necessity) leads to affirming khawāriq.
4
Examine the proof for occurrence
The proof is the story of Mary (Maryam). She conceived without a male, received sustenance without a cause, and had dates fall. This is a supernatural event for a saint, so miracles occur.
The story is from the Qur'an, showing that scripture confirms such events.
5
Reflect on the editorial note
The passage ends with a note about al-Razi's report: whether the denial is of permissibility or just occurrence. This clarifies the scope of disagreement.
Think about why this distinction matters for the overall argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد التاسع : في كرامات الأولياء ] ( في كرامات الأولياء وإنها جائزة عندنا خلافاً لمن منع جواز الخوارق ( واقعة خلافاً للاستاذ أبي إسحاق والحليمي منا وغير أبي الحسين من المعتزلة) قال الإمام الرازي في الأربعين : المعتزلة ينكرون كرامات الأولياء ووافقهم الأستاذ أبو إسحاق منا وأكثر أصحابنا يثبتونها وبه قال أبو الحسين البصري من المعتزلة لنا إما جوازها فظاهر على أصولنا ) وهي أن وجود الممكنات مستند إلى قدرته الشاملة لجميعها فلا يمتنع شيء منها على قدرته ولا يجب غرض في أفعاله ولا شك أن الكرامة أمر ممكن، إذ ليس يلزم من فرض وقوعها محال لذاته ( وإما وقوعها فلقصة مريم ) رضي الله عنها حيث حملت بلا ذكر ووجد الرزق عندها بلا سبب وتساقط عليها الرطب . قوله : (قال الإمام الرازي في الأربعين إلخ ) الظاهر من قوله ينكرون كرامات الأولياء أنهم ينكرون جوازها، ففائدة النقل على هذا ظاهر ولك أن تجعل فائدة بيان أن الخلاف المذكور في المتن قيد الوقوع لا الجواز .
The Ninth Section: On the Miracles of Saints. (On the miracles of saints: that they are permissible according to us, contrary to those who forbid the occurrence of supernatural events; and that they occur, contrary to al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq and al-Halimi among us, and others like Abu al-Husayn from the Mu'tazila). Imam al-Razi said in al-Arba'in: The Mu'tazila deny the miracles of saints, and al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq among us agreed with them. Most of our companions affirm them, and Abu al-Husayn al-Basri from the Mu'tazila also held this view. Our proof: As for their permissibility, it is apparent from our principles: the existence of possibles is dependent on His power encompassing all of them, so nothing is impossible for His power, and there is no necessity of purpose in His actions. There is no doubt that the miracle (karama) is possible, for it does not entail an impossibility in itself. As for their occurrence, [we have] the story of Mary (may Allah be pleased with her) when she conceived without a male, and sustenance was found with her without a cause, and dates fell upon her. His statement: 'Imam al-Razi said in al-Arba'in etc.' The apparent meaning of his saying 'they deny the miracles of saints' is that they deny their permissibility. So the benefit of the transmission is clear in this regard. But you may also make its benefit that the disagreement mentioned in the text is restricted to occurrence, not permissibility.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage introduces the ninth section on the miracles of saints (karāmāt al-awliyā'). It first states the Ash'ari position: such miracles are permissible (jāʾiz) and actually occur (wāqiʿa). It notes that some groups deny them: some Mu'tazila, and among the Ash'aris, Abu Ishaq and al-Halimi. It then cites al-Razi's mention of the disagreement. The proof for permissibility is based on Ash'ari principles: all possible things are subject to God's power, which has no limitations. There is no logical impossibility in the occurrence of a miracle, so it is possible. As for actual occurrence, the story of Mary (Maryam) is cited: she conceived without a male, received sustenance without a cause, and had dates fall upon her. These are clear examples of supernatural events for a saint. The editorial note at the end clarifies that al-Razi's report about the Mu'tazila denying karāmāt likely refers to denying permissibility, but one could interpret it as denying only occurrence.

Key Terms
كرامات الأولياء
جواز
وقوع
الخوارق
قصة مريم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Ash'aris deny saintly miracles or limit them to prophets only.
Correction: The Ash'ari school as presented here affirms both the possibility and actual occurrence of saintly miracles, based on God's unlimited power and evidence from the Qur'an (story of Mary).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Ash'ari proof for the permissibility (jawāz) of the miracles of saints?
A) The consensus of the Companions
B) The story of Mary
C) The fact that all possibles are within God's power and no impossibility is entailed
D) The hadith on the humility of saints

Key Takeaway
Saintly miracles are both possible (based on God's power) and actual (evidenced by Mary's story) in Ash'ari theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted God's power in a situation where all natural means were absent? What would it mean for you to truly believe that He can provide without any cause, as He did for Mary?
?
When you read the story of Mary, do you see it as a distant historical event or as a living proof that God still works through saints today? What would change in your life if you expected such interventions?
?
The lesson shows that some learned scholars denied the occurrence of saintly miracles. Are there any teachings or leaders you have trusted that might have weakened your conviction in God's absolute power? How will you guard your heart against such doubts?
